  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>I am running Derby 10.9.1.0 and am trying to figure out a performance problem with query taking too long. I don’t actually want to run the query so from the documentation, I try:</p> 
                  <p>call syscs_util.syscs_set_runtimestatistics(1);<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_schema('STATS');<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(1);<br> — my query here<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_runtimestatistics(0);<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_schema('');<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(0);</p> 
                  <p>When it runs my query, I get:</p> 
                  <p>ERROR XCL16: ResultSet not open. Operation 'getMetaData' not permitted. Verify that autocommit is OFF.</p> 
                  <p>I try the following with IJ just to see:</p> 
                  <p>call syscs_util.syscs_set_runtimestatistics(1);<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_schema('STATS');<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(1);<br> select sql_text from syscs_diag.transaction_table where status != 'IDLE';<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_runtimestatistics(0);<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_schema('');<br> call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(0);</p> 
                  <p>Note I have tried this with real tables as apposed to the syscs_diag.transaction_table with the same result. The only reason that I posted this with this table is that it is a table that is accessible for any database.</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe statement that was compiled before xplain was enabled actually behaved as desired. It returned results if xplain mode was disabled, and returned empty results if it was enabled. I think this statement works because BasicNoPutResultSetImpl.getNextRow() still checks the LCC instead of the local flag. (Note: this was in getNextRow(), not in getNextRowCore().)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe statement that was compiled when xplain was enabled, on the other hand, continued returning empty results even after xplain had been disabled. It might be a problem that the flag is set in the constructor, though. The constructor is only called the first time a PreparedStatement is executed, so it may cause some surprises if the same statement is used both with xplain mode enabled and disabled. \\n\\n Example ij session: \\n\\n ij version 10.11 \\nij&gt; connect \'jdbc:derby:memory:db;create=true\'; \\nij&gt; prepare ps1 as \'values \'\'Compiled before xplain mode was enabled\'\'\'; \\nij&gt; execute ps1; \\n1                                       \\n--------------------------------------- \\nCompiled before xplain mode was enabled \\n\\n 1 row selected \\nij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_runtimestatistics(1); \\n0 rows inserted\\/updated\\/deleted \\nij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_schema(\'STATS\'); \\n0 rows inserted\\/updated\\/deleted \\nij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(1); \\n0 rows inserted\\/updated\\/deleted \\nij&gt; execute ps1; \\n1                                       \\n--------------------------------------- \\n\\n 0 rows selected \\nij&gt; prepare ps2 as \'values \'\'Compiled when xplain mode was enabled\'\'\'; \\nij&gt; execute ps2; \\n1                                     \\n------------------------------------- \\n\\n 0 rows selected \\nij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_runtimestatistics(0); \\n0 rows inserted\\/updated\\/deleted \\nij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_schema(\'\'); \\n0 rows inserted\\/updated\\/deleted \\nij&gt; call syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(0); \\n0 rows inserted\\/updated\\/deleted \\nij&gt; execute ps1; \\n1                                       \\n--------------------------------------- \\nCompiled before xplain mode was enabled \\n\\n 1 row selected \\nij&gt; execute ps2; \\n1                                     \\n------------------------------------- \\n\\n 0 rows selected \\nij&gt;  \\n\\n\\n The statement that was compiled before xplain was enabled actually behaved as desired. It returned results if xplain mode was disabled, and returned empty results if it was enabled. I think this statement works because BasicNoPutResultSetImpl.getNextRow() still checks the LCC instead of the local flag. (Note: this was in getNextRow(), not in getNextRowCore().) \\n\\n The statement that was compiled when xplain was enabled, on the other hand, continued returning empty results even after xplain had been disabled. I think it would be more reasonable if it had returned results after disabling xplain mode. \\n\\n I think it might work better if the flag is initialized in open() instead of the constructor. \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt might be that caching the xplain-only flag is premature optimization, and that it would be better in the first increment to check the flag via the lcc on each call to getNextRowCore(). I\'d expect that to make it easier to get the correct behaviour and write tests whose results are easier to understand. When we have well-behaved tests for the feature, it may be easier to introduce optimizations later without breaking anything.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe patch attempts to reset the flag in the reopenCore() method. It looks like many subclasses override that method without calling super.reopenCore(), so that may not be the most robust place for it.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf we are to cache the value in BasicNoPutResultSetImpl\\/NoPutResultSetImpl, I\'m wondering if it might be better if the flag has three possible values: true, false, unknown. The flag is initialized to unknown in the constructor. If getNextRowCore() sees that it is unknown, it initializes by looking up the value in the lcc. The flag could be reset to unknown in close(). (Of course, it still has the weakness that subclasses that override close() must remember to call super.close(), but at least that requirement is called out in NoPutResultSetImpl.close()\'s javadoc comment, so it\'s a bug if a class doesn\'t already do that.)\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"knutanders\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13697864_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=knutanders\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"knutanders\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Knut Anders Hatlen\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13697864_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Jul\\/13 15:10\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-07-02T15:10:05+0000\'\u003e02\\/Jul\\/13 15:10\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    It might be that caching the xplain-only flag is premature optimization, and that it would be better in the first increment to check the flag via the lcc on each call to getNextRowCore(). I\'d expect that to make it easier to get the correct behaviour and write tests whose results are easier to understand. When we have well-behaved tests for the feature, it may be easier to introduce optimizations later without breaking anything. \\n\\n The patch attempts to reset the flag in the reopenCore() method. It looks like many subclasses override that method without calling super.reopenCore(), so that may not be the most robust place for it. \\n\\n If we are to cache the value in BasicNoPutResultSetImpl\\/NoPutResultSetImpl, I\'m wondering if it might be better if the flag has three possible values: true, false, unknown. The flag is initialized to unknown in the constructor. If getNextRowCore() sees that it is unknown, it initializes by looking up the value in the lcc. The flag could be reset to unknown in close(). (Of course, it still has the weakness that subclasses that override close() must remember to call super.close(), but at least that requirement is called out in NoPutResultSetImpl.close()\'s javadoc comment, so it\'s a bug if a class doesn\'t already do that.)              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_13707754_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'13\\/Jul\\/13 15:02\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2013-07-13T15:02:43+0000\'\u003e13\\/Jul\\/13 15:02\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Commit 1502795 from  Bryan Pendleton  \\n[  https:\\/\\/svn.apache.org\\/r1502795  ] \\n\\n   DERBY-6216  : XPLAIN feature does not work, gives XCL16: ResultSet not open \\n\\n This change adjusts the implementation of the explain-only mode feature, \\nwhich is enabled via syscs_util.syscs_set_xplain_mode(1). \\n\\n Prior to this change, the implementation short-circuited the open() method \\nof the ResultSet classes, causing the execution engine to terminate \\nimmediately because the result sets were not open. \\n\\n This change takes an alternate approach, suggested by Knut Anders: the open() \\nis allowed to proceed normally, but we short-circuit the getNextRow() \\nmethod of the ResultSet classes. This way, the result sets all appear to be \\nnormal result sets, open and ready for business, but they do no work and \\nalways produce an empty result. \\n\\n Then, at the end of the execution, the statistics are gathered. They show \\nthat no work was done, but they contain information about the overall \\\"shape\\\" \\nof the query plan (which result sets were constructed, and what the overall \\nresult set tree looks like). \\n\\n We also discovered that we were completely missing regression tests for the \\nexplain-only feature, so this change adds a handful of regression tests, \\nincluding an IJ-based test, a simple embedded query, and a test that verifies \\nthat explain-only mode can be turned on and off between executions of a \\nprepared query. \\n\\n More testing would clearly be beneficial, but this should at least give us \\na feature that basically works.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n
